< Review>
I first visited this service centre six years ago. I purchased new updated aids there two years ago. I have found the product to be exceptional. But the service far outweighs the product. I have lost one aid while in Canada and had a replacement within a very few days of calling the office. Upon returning south this fall I visited the office and had the aids checked and retuned. <Text>This old school gem is tucked in to the northwest corner of Pasadena near the Eagle Rock border. The menu offers traditional Italian fare, and the daily specials are not to be missed. There is a full bar, with live piano during the latter part of the week. And, the Service is outstanding. In the three years that we have lived here, we have never had an experience which fell short of excellent. This has become our "go-to" local restaurant, and it is a pleasure to support this small local business.<//Text>< Pictures>

<Name>A C< /Name><review>My wife and I came here for dinner today. Upon entering, the two of us were seated at a table side by side (the other side only had room for a chair positioned for the next table behind). I saw someone who I think may have been the owner, who gave us what felt like a very judgmental look (perhaps as we were the youngest there?), but notably I have never commented on noticing something like this from any of my other reviews. I also noticed a paucity of interaction between waiters and patrons.
The food order was incorrect, we asked for the sauteed chicken with pine nuts but were instead given the sauteed chicken with lemon sauce. Partly as I wasn't expecting it, the lemon component was extremely overpowering for the chicken  dish, but I'm not one to have them cook up new food for any of the above reasons. Chicken was clearly originally frozen.
The lasagna dish was okay but tasted like something that came out of a Kroger box.
I was expecting more for the price point of Stoney.
The clams were tasty, and our waiter was very friendly, hence the 2nd star.</review><pics>None< /pics>< rate>

< Review>
Don't order the vegetarian burrito unless you like just rice and cheese maybe tortilla. So much jiggly grizzle bits in the asada. And I got the shrimp burrito with 3.5 shrimp. (Update: I dug out two other shrimp from the remnants of the burrito) And then they said there was no chicken, and then there was a piece of chicken in some ones burrito. Burritos advertised with sour cream and guac, none to be found except for the burrito that requested no guac. The big red flag was that we were the only four people in that restaurant. Oh and I don't know what happened but their liquor license is suspended. Two stars for the delicious salsa and chips. And one for the really nice lady who brought us "food".< /Review>

<name>Michael Kovac</name><Date>1548054000219<//Date>< rating>

< Text>
In short, Charcoal is one of the best restaurants in LA. With a two-star Chef/Owner Josiah Citrin, you've got a menu filled with some of the most delicious, craveable food - all tinged with the flavor of a charcoal grill. Want proof? Start with brunch and their ridiculously addictive Charcoal Baked Potato stuffed with a poached egg, sour cream, and smoked Gouda. Sounds simple, but it's perfection. Ditto for the Smoked Salmon Benedict with a charcoal toned Hollandaise sauce. The house smoked salmon is spectacular. And if you've got a kid or a sweet tooth, order the Dutch Baby Blueberry Pancake that's served in a skillet with a side of  vanilla whipped cream and blueberry compote. It's guaranteed to disappear quickly.<//Text>

<rate>4</rate>< text>
A more casual, but still hip spot, by the people that brought you Melisse. As the name implies most of the items on the menu are grilled or charcoal cooked. It's a little loud, it's a little cozy and it's a little expensive. Not quite a steakhouse, but as much as the menu seems to lean towards protein, the highlights and standouts are the veggies.

The coal roasted cabbage is a mainstay appetizer and for good reason. Fork tender but still has structure, paired with the yogurt, sumac, lemon; it is a simple but yet sophisticated dish. The roasted carrots had a slight, bitter char that was eased by the creamy and cool sheep ricotta cheese. The seasonal sunchokes were tender and ate like a cross between artichokes and a fingerling potato; the meter lemon scallion dressing had a good blend of umami and acidity.

The large striploin for 2 was 20 oz and perfectly cooked medium rare in the charcoals. A little under seasoned for my taste, but I suspect it was because of the optional sauces of house made herb vinegar, chimichurri, smokey BBQ sauce and house A1/honey mustard (not a fan of the last two).

Suggested attire is business casual, but it's by the beach so a little more casual than that is okay. Cocktails are $15, wine by the glass are in the ~$16 range, beers in the $8/9 range.

I can see the appeal and it's a good modern alternative to your standard, fancier steak houses. Will be back to check out happy hour which is 5:30-7:00pm nightly at the bar.< /text>

< text>
Great food, super vibe, really busy.  We tried Charcoal on the Dine LA menu.  What a great value.  We added a couple of appetizers just to try some more items.  Overall it was wonderful.  The Flat Iron Steak was as tender as a filet, but with a ton more taste.  The appetizers were a treat.  I loved the barbecued chicken drumettes.  The cabbage appetizer was a real surprise.  It is not often that I can say that I love cabbage.  My only negative was the fact that we ordered an extra butter with our bread, and they charged us $2.95.  When I asked about it, the waiter took it off our check without me requesting the removal.  Really smart staff, smart manager and great cooking.  Innovative, creative, high quality, a great dining experience.  I highly recommend Charcoal.</text>

< Text>
I come to this spot every time I visit LA. Try to get a reservation because it can be crowded, but I've had no trouble finding a spot at the bar. Place is fairly spendy, but you get what you pay for: Top-notch cocktails and wines with food you've never tasted before, especially if you like a charcoal smokey flavor. It's infused into just about everything. Go for a nice steak and don't skip on getting the chicken wings. Kitchen is open, so you can see right in and the atmosphere is elegant, but casual. Staff is great, too. I'll be back!<//Text>

< review>
My wife has been commenting for some time that she would like to try this place. I surprised her for our anniversary and made a reservation (place is always busy so make a reservation). We arrived on time and were seated in about 5 minutes. In my reservation I had mentioned it was our anniversary and my wife has Celiac disease. Everyone wished us a happy anniversary and there was even a cute card on our table. They also took my wife's food allergy seriously and seemed well trained to be aware.
The food is amazing and the service equally amazing and attentive.
This place is designed around sharing, a mistake we made not knowing. We had the ribeye, carrot and steak fries as well as the strawberry fields and old fashioned drinks and the apple crumble (which was gluten free). Everything was so good!! Special props to Sara our great server who was funny, friendly and just all around great.</review>

<Time>1502176119094</Time>< review>
This is one of the best restaurants I have ever been to. My sister picked out this place on our first trip to LA and by the end of our trip, we cancelled our reservations elsewhere, we came back to Charcoal Venice for a second time.

The food is absolutely incredible and worth every penny. The first time we began with the cabbage and the second time with the bread and French butter. Both were outstanding. We had the skirt steak both times because it was some of the best we've ever had.

We both were extremely impressed with the staff, as well. They all worked together so well and helped look after each others tables. They were all so kind and so efficient. I've never seen anything like it. The manager was so on top of things and helped the staff out so much.

All in all, if you go to Venice, don't skip over this place. You won't regret it. Excellent staff and wonderful food. We will absolutely be back!< /review>

<Review>Don't believe the hype.  This place should be a lot better, especially for the price. The food ranges from okay to pretty good,  but definitely avoid the steak.  I've had three different types of steak,  each on different occasions,  ranging from the cheapest to the higher end.  They were all woefully underwhelming and the meat itself lacks so much flavor it's hard to distinguish which was better.  Sure you can douse it in a sauce,  but having the meat by itself,  aside from the salt and admittedly nice charcoal flavor on the outside,  the actual meat is flavorless.  He needs to find a better source for his cows. < name>
TReed White< /name>
<Date>1559003672554<//Date>< rate>
5</rate>
< text>
Charcoal has become a destination restaurant. We have friends who come here from Miami Beach, FL who make Charcoal their main destination. The restaurant's unique (and very pricey menu) offers charcoal grilled meats and vegetables.  Some standout side items: the char-grilled cabbage with yoghurt sauce, the smoked German potatoes with onions and mushrooms, the char-grilled carrots with yoghurt. The duck and chicken are very good, but the fish was too salty for our tastes. However, the MAIN reason to eat at Charcoal is the char-grilled red meats. The Skirt Steak, the Hangar Steak are delicious, and though some think the lean Bison Steak ($60) is THE reason to eat at Charcoal, we disagree. We have found the other red meats more satisfying and less expensive. If you like lemonade, they have a berry one with is also char-flavored. They also make signature cocktails. If you are into desserts and love Olive Oil Cake as much as we do, they make a very lovely one. But try the Chocolate Crisp Peanut Butter Cake. The Apple Crumb is also very good. All-in-all, Charcoal is expensive, but worth the spluge for a unique dining experience. The place is VERY popular; reservations are necessary, and you will be charged a No-Show fee if you make one but not everyone in your party shows up. This is now a common practice for high-end, very busy restaurants. The place is noisy, so it is not suited to a quiet romantic dinner. The best choice is for a group of six ppl to come and everyone at the table order something different to share. Wait staff is helpful and eager to answer queries.<//text>

<gmapID>0x80c2bb2e705c8d5f:0x5a4d7eb59b884fba</gmapID><review>Wowza! This is my second time ... this time, via Uber Eats. My first visit was spectacular, this one was too ... but a few things of note for both sides. I was hungry, so for a big order, I went right for the Lamb Ribs ... I might have to say they might be the best lamb ribs I've ever had! They had some very unique seasoning, I believe they were smoked, and oh so good .... they didn't taste like lamb at all oddly, but still, just delicious .... a little fatty, but that might be why they were so tender ... Next, chopped salad, most excellent, a lot of stuff in there, maybe too much, but very good, .... seemed like a healthy and crunchy choice of fresh stuff - not off the charts like the ribs, but good. THE STEAK! Hmmm ... most excellent, but I ordered it medium rare. I would recommend it medium. The steak is VERY marbled, which is good ... but with all that marbling, the fat and gristle needs to be cooked down a bit more than medium rare in IMHO ... it was a bit too chewy and fatty at medium rare. I heated it a bit more myself on my cast iron pan and it was much, much better at medium. It was a great piece of meat, but I would like a tiny bit more seasoning, if only just some salt, but again, good meat. The collards .... they were not as expected, most folks have them more old school, e.g well cooked down .... these were raw or maybe barely cooked, very good, but not what I expected. I would not have added all the bread crumbs and cheese, would have been nicer to have them a little more simple and light, delicious, but with the added things in there, a bit heavy. A couple of little nit pics, but all in all the food was outstanding ... order 2 orders of the lamb ribs, ribeye medium, and a few more dishes and you'll be a happy fan! I will be back again and even if by Uber Eats, "I'll be back"! Oh .... bonus points: I'm not always a fan of "steak sauce" but oh my oh my, their sauce, I think it's called J-1 (??), it was fantastic!!!! I nice tang of home-made goodness, I wonder if they sell it by the bottle??? It's that good. See ya'll soon, great work, delicious!</review>< Resp>

Jason Lee</user_name>
<time>1452480231413<//time><Rate>5<//Rate>< review>
Stunner on Washington Blvd.  Beautiful food, attentive service, and casual but sophisticated atmosphere makes this restaurant a must-stop for a nice dinner.  Namesake - grilled - meats, fish, and vegetable matched with modern cocktails (some nice interpretations of old school cocktails), an interesting, curated, mid-to-high end (but not steak house) wine list made our meal memorable.  Aged-35-day duck was pricey (and our server warned us that the although the portion size indicated a half duck, be prepared for a de-boned portion that may cause you to wonder about the near $50 you just spent) but - yes - worth it.  If the quality keeps up as the restaurant matures, will be a stalwart in what otherwise is a bit of a deadzone (and graveyard to many other restaurants).</review>

<UserId.>107225128838203487504< /UserId.><username>Thomas Hollier< /username><Time>1452539590788<//Time><rating>1<//rating>< text>
From long time Venice resident and KCRW music DJ Tom Schnabel:

At my ripe old age not that many firsts happen, but last night was an exception. I was thrown out of a restaurant.
I was happy to see Josiah Citrin's (of M√©lisse and Guide Michelin fame) new space Charcoal finally open on Washington Blvd. I even attended a community meeting last fall to voice my approval of this new high-end eatery, one of the few within walking distance of my flat.
While waiting near the bar for a table to open up, I was bumped and pushed by some stranger; I thought to myself 'what's up with that guy'. Then my friend Joe walked by him and, the aisle being quite narrow, his jacket brushed up against the same guy that had pushed me. The guy pushed my friend back in retaliation. My friend is not one to be pushed around, and a fight almost ensued.
Then the manager then came and asked us to leave. Turns out, the belligerent jerk was a big investor. And apparently he enjoyed his power, pushing people around at Charcoal. Even one of the hostesses told us he'd done the same to her. When we refused to leave, Charcoal's manager said he'd call the police.
Needless to say, this ruined our dinner and I don't plan on returning to Charcoal anytime soon. Just because you're a major investor in the new restaurant, that doesn't justify being boorish and rude with patrons like me and my two guests.
So we left Charcoal and walked next door to Le Cellier, a French-Vietnamese bistro that had a calmer, more welcoming ambience, and enjoyed a nice meal together.< /text>

<text>Valley Vapes unfortunately leans on the shady side of sales. They have a habit of under-quoting prices then overcharging on the receipt. It's happened a number of times but $5-10 here and there wasn't worth burning a bridge with the closest local shop. (Prices are not marked in the store so you're cost is up to them)
A while back I picked up 2 new tanks, a pack of coils for each, a couple 30mils and a "Fuchai 213" by Sigelei. I'm not heavy into the vape community, I simply use the devices so I rely heavily on what I'd expect to be a professional within one's industry.
I was quoted $100 for the mod and confirmed it was a good choice. After swiping the card, it was naturally $10 over the quote, where the tanks were $3-4 over the quote... who knows how much of a premium was tagged onto the other products. I did receive $19 in "discounts" from my rewards number.
Once I got home, I looked the mod up on Youtube for a full rundown on the controls and immediately saw just about everywhere online selling for $48 with free shipping (some as high as 70 with 'free' Sony cells). A little frustrating but I'd rather support local business and understand online shops often sell near dealer cost. Youtube had a slew of negative demos where the temp control was faulty, the USB was charge only (no firmware updates), charging port balancing issues, over-claimed wattage, etc.
I felt a bit taken for a ride. I can't help but think not only are prices bumped at will, but they were also well aware the device had issues and wanted to move them. I called no more than an hour or so after purchasing to see if we could make things right. "No returns, no exchanges, all sales final." I have my suspicions the gentleman I spoke to on the phone was the same that rang me up but he claimed to had not been there when the mod was sold and that he'd have to talk to his manager and have "him" call me back.
I was the only person in the shop aside from a young lady laying down on the couch. I can appreciate there's often plenty of work to be done off of the sales floor so I gave it a few hours to see if I get a call back before posting. Call never came.

Long story short, if you plan on trying out Valley Vape:
1) Do not buy products on the whim (Don't rely on their "expertise").
2) Know what you're after and the average brick & mortar going rate.
3) Ask for prices before picking products AND before paying to ensure they match up. Record the audio if need be (seriously, it's that bad...)
4) Honestly, I'd suggest shopping elsewhere. This isn't an honest company and truly does not deserve your business.< /text>< pictures>
None</pictures>

Great shop. I quit smoking and went in for a vape.
